<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Spider-Man 3</i></h1>

<p><i><b>Spider-Man 3</b></i> is a 2007 American <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel Entertainment</a> and Laura Ziskin Productions, and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fictional_character" title="Fictional character">fictional</a> <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> character <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Spider-Man</a>. It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi</a> and scripted by Sam and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Raimi" title="Ivan Raimi">Ivan Raimi</a> and Alvin Sargent. It is the final film in the <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film" title="Spider-Man in film">Sam Raimi <i>Spider-Man</i> trilogy</a>. The film stars <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Dunst" title="Kirsten Dunst">Kirsten Dunst</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Haden_Church" title="Thomas Haden Church">Thomas Haden Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Topher_Grace" title="Topher Grace">Topher Grace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryce_Dallas_Howard" title="Bryce Dallas Howard">Bryce Dallas Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosemary_Harris" title="Rosemary Harris">Rosemary Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._K._Simmons" title="J. K. Simmons">J. K. Simmons</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Cromwell" title="James Cromwell">James Cromwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Robertson" title="Cliff Robertson">Cliff Robertson</a> in his final film appearance.</p>
<p>Set months after the events of <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Peter Parker</a> has become a cultural phenomenon as Spider-Man, while <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">Mary Jane Watson</a> continues her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" title="Broadway theater">Broadway</a> career. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">Harry Osborn</a> still seeks vengeance for his father's death, and an escaped <a href="/wiki/Sandman_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Sandman (Marvel Comics)">Flint Marko</a> falls into a <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle accelerator</a> and is transformed into a shape-shifting sand manipulator. An <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrials_in_fiction" title="Extraterrestrials in fiction">extraterrestrial</a> <a href="/wiki/Symbiote_(comics)" title="Symbiote (comics)">symbiote</a> crashes to Earth and bonds with Peter, influencing his behavior for the worst.</p>
<p>Development of <i>Spider-Man 3</i> began immediately after the release of <i>Spider-Man 2</i> for a 2007 release. During pre-production, Raimi originally wanted another villain to be included along with Sandman, but at the request of producer <a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a>, the director added <a href="/wiki/Venom_(comics)" title="Venom (comics)">Venom</a> and the producers also requested the addition of <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stacy" title="Gwen Stacy">Gwen Stacy</a>. Principal photography for the film began in January 2006, and took place in Los Angeles and Cleveland, before moving to New York City from May until July 2006. Additional pick-up shots were made after August and the film wrapped in October 2006. During post-production, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Imageworks" title="Sony Pictures Imageworks">Sony Pictures Imageworks</a> created 900 visual effects shots.</p>
<p><i>Spider-Man 3</i> premiered on April 16, 2007 in Tokyo, and was released in the United States in both conventional and <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters on May 4, 2007. Unlike the predecessors, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> reviews from critics were mixed to positive, who felt it lacked a focused or substantial plot due to the excessive presence of characters from the comic books; however, it stands as the most financially successful film in the series worldwide, Marvel's third most financially successful film after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">Sony Pictures Entertainment</a>'s second highest-grossing film behind <i><a href="/wiki/Skyfall" title="Skyfall">Skyfall</a></i>, despite being <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_films" title="List of most expensive films">the most expensive film of all time</a> at release (the record was surpassed just three weeks later by <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i>).</p>
<p>After the commercial success of <i>Spider-Man 3</i>, Raimi was scheduled to direct a fourth film. However, disagreements between Sony and Raimi forced the director to leave the project, and Sony canceled the film as a result. <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">A reboot</a> of the trilogy was released five years later.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Peter Parker plans to propose to Mary Jane Watson, who has just made her Broadway musical debut. A meteorite crashes near the two in Central Park, and an extraterrestrial symbiote attaches itself to Peter's moped. While fleeing police, escaped prisoner Flint Marko falls into a particle accelerator that fuses his DNA with surrounding sand, allowing him to shapeshift at will as the Sandman. Peter's best friend, Harry Osborn, who blames him for his father's death, attacks Peter using weapons based on his father's Green Goblin technology. Harry injures his head and suffers partial amnesia, forgetting that Peter is Spider-Man and his desire for revenge. During a festival honouring Spider-Man, Marko robs an armored car. NYPD Captain George Stacy tells Peter and Aunt May that Marko was Uncle Ben's killer, and Dennis Carradine was only an accomplice. While a vengeful Peter sleeps, the symbiote bonds with him. Peter wakes up hanging from a skyscraper. His costume becomes black and his powers increase, but the symbiote brings out Peter's dark side. Wearing the new suit, Spider-Man locates Marko and battles him in a subway tunnel, reducing him to mud using water.</p>
<p>Mary Jane, whose career is floundering, is humiliated by Peter's changed personality and finds solace with Harry. Urged on by a hallucination of his father, Harry regains his memory and blackmails Mary Jane into breaking up with Peter. At Harry's direction, Mary Jane tells Peter she loves another man. Harry meets with Peter and claims to be "the other guy". Later, Peter, wearing the black suit, confronts Harry. Harry throws a pumpkin bomb at Peter, who deflects it back, disfiguring Harry's face.</p>
<p>Under the symbiote's influence, Peter exposes Eddie Brock, a rival photographer at the <i>Daily Bugle</i>, for submitting doctored photographs painting Spider-Man as a criminal. Furious at having to print a retraction, J. Jonah Jameson dismisses Eddie. To make Mary Jane jealous, Peter brings Gwen Stacy, Brock's ex girlfriend, to the nightclub where Mary Jane works; Brock sees them and assumes they are dating. Gwen catches on and storms out. Peter brawls with the bouncers, and after mistakenly hitting Mary Jane, he realizes the symbiote is changing him. He retreats to a church bell tower. While trying to remove the symbiote costume, Peter hits the church's bell, causing sonic vibrations that weaken the alien, making it easier to remove. The symbiote falls to the lower tower, landing on Brock, who is praying for Peter's death. The symbiote transforms Brock into Venom, and while initially horrified, he gleefully accepts his new form. Venom finds the Sandman and offers to join forces.</p>
<p>Mary Jane hails a taxi but Brock hijacks it and hangs it from a web above a sand-filled construction site. Peter seeks Harry's help but is rejected. However, Harry learns the truth about his father's death from his butler and decides to help Peter, who is battling Venom and the Sandman at the construction site. Peter, overwhelmed by the villains, is on the brink of being killed when Harry arrives. Harry subdues a gigantic incarnation of the Sandman, breaking him apart. Venom webs Harry's glider, causing him to bump into some pipes, making sonic vibrations that weaken the symbiote; Peter recalls the church bells weakening it previously. Venom tries impaling Peter with Harry's glider, but Harry jumps in the way and is fatally wounded. Peter forms a ring of pipes around Venom, creating a wall of sonic vibrations. The alien releases Brock, and Peter pulls Brock away from the symbiote. Peter throws a pumpkin bomb from Harry's glider at the symbiote, but Brock jumps back into the symbiote and both are killed.</p>
<p>Marko reveals that he never intended to kill Ben; he only wanted his car and accidentally shot him when Dennis grabbed his arm. Ben's death has haunted him ever since. Peter forgives Marko, who dissolves into sand and floats away. Peter and Harry forgive each other before Harry dies with Mary Jane and Peter at his side. A few days later, Peter, Mary Jane, and Aunt May attend Harry's funeral. Peter later visits the jazz club where Mary Jane is singing, and they begin mending their relationship.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a> as <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Spider-Man / Peter Parker</a>: A superhero, brilliant <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> student at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>, and photographer for the <i>Daily Bugle</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Dunst" title="Kirsten Dunst">Kirsten Dunst</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">Mary Jane Watson</a>: Peter's girlfriend, whom he has loved since childhood.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a> as <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">New Goblin / Harry Osborn</a>: The dedicated son of Norman Osborn, and Peter's estranged best friend, who believes Spider-Man murdered his father. After learning Peter is Spider-Man and his father was the Green Goblin, Harry becomes the New Goblin to battle Peter directly.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Haden_Church" title="Thomas Haden Church">Thomas Haden Church</a> as <a href="/wiki/Sandman_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Sandman (Marvel Comics)">Sandman / Flint Marko</a>: A small-time thug with an estranged wife and sick daughter. He robs to get enough money to get his daughter treatment. He becomes the Sandman following a freak accident, and is hunted by Peter when he learns Marko was Ben Parker's true killer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Topher_Grace" title="Topher Grace">Topher Grace</a> as <a href="/wiki/Venom_(comics)" title="Venom (comics)">Venom</a> / <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Brock" title="Eddie Brock">Eddie Brock</a>: Peter's rival at the <i>Daily Bugle</i>. He is exposed by Peter for creating a fake image of Spider-Man, and is ready for revenge when he bonds with the symbiote.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bryce_Dallas_Howard" title="Bryce Dallas Howard">Bryce Dallas Howard</a> as <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stacy" title="Gwen Stacy">Gwen Stacy</a>: Peter's lab partner and good friend, who is also saved by Spider-Man.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosemary_Harris" title="Rosemary Harris">Rosemary Harris</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/May_Parker" title="May Parker">May Parker</a>: Peter's aunt. She gives Peter her <a href="/wiki/Engagement_ring" title="Engagement ring">engagement ring</a> so he can propose to Mary Jane, and teaches him forgiveness.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J._K._Simmons" title="J. K. Simmons">J. K. Simmons</a> as <a href="/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson" title="J. Jonah Jameson">J. Jonah Jameson</a>: The aggressive chief of the <i>Daily Bugle</i>. He despises Spider-Man.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Cromwell" title="James Cromwell">James Cromwell</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_George_Stacy" title="Captain George Stacy">Captain George Stacy</a>: Gwen's father and a <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">New York City Police Department</a> Captain.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Theresa_Russell" title="Theresa Russell">Theresa Russell</a> as Emma Marko: Flint's wife.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dylan_Baker" title="Dylan Baker">Dylan Baker</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Curt_Connors" title="Dr. Curt Connors">Dr. Curt Connors</a>: Peter's college physics professor. He examines a piece of the symbiote and tells Peter it "amplifies characteristics of its hostâ¦ especially aggression."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Nunn" title="Bill Nunn">Bill Nunn</a> as <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Robertson_(comics)" title="Robbie Robertson (comics)">Joseph "Robbie" Robertson</a>: A longtime employee at the <i>Daily Bugle</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Banks" title="Elizabeth Banks">Elizabeth Banks</a> as <a href="/wiki/Betty_Brant" title="Betty Brant">Betty Brant</a>: Jameson's Receptionist at the <i>Daily Bugle</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ted_Raimi" title="Ted Raimi">Ted Raimi</a> as Hoffman: A <i>Daily Bugle</i> employee who suggests a catchphrase to Jameson.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Perla_Haney-Jardine" title="Perla Haney-Jardine">Perla Haney-Jardine</a> as Penny Marko: Flint and Emma's sick daughter.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Willem_Dafoe" title="Willem Dafoe">Willem Dafoe</a> as <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">Norman Osborn / Green Goblin</a>: Harry's dead father returns as a hallucination to encourage his son to destroy Spider-Man.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cliff_Robertson" title="Cliff Robertson">Cliff Robertson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Ben" title="Uncle Ben">Ben Parker</a>: Peter Parker's deceased uncle.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elya_Baskin" title="Elya Baskin">Elya Baskin</a> as Dr. Ditkovitch: Peter's landlord.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mageina_Tovah" title="Mageina Tovah">Mageina Tovah</a> as Ursula Ditkovich: The unassuming daughter of Dr. Ditkovitch.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Papajohn" title="Michael Papajohn">Michael Papajohn</a> as <a href="/wiki/Burglar_(comics)" title="Burglar (comics)">Dennis Carradine</a>: The carjacker who was believed to have murdered Uncle Ben.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Manganiello" title="Joe Manganiello">Joe Manganiello</a> as Flash Thompson: Mary Jane's boyfriend in the first <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film)" title="Spider-Man (2002 film)">Spider-Man</a></i> film, he reprises his role in a silent cameo where he attends Harry's funeral.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameos">Cameos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cameos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Spider-Man co-creator <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a> has a cameo in <i>Spider-Man 3</i>, as he does in many <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel</a>-based films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He plays a man who, after reading a news bulletin along with Peter, tells him, "You know, I guess one person can make a difference", followed by his catchphrase "'Nuff said." Actor <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Campbell" title="Bruce Campbell">Bruce Campbell</a>, who had cameo roles as a <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_ring" title="Wrestling ring">wrestling ring</a> announcer in <i>Spider-Man</i> and as a rude usher in <i>Spider-Man 2</i>, returns in <i>Spider-Man 3</i> with a new cameo as a French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ma%C3%AEtre_d%27" title="MaÃ®tre d'">maÃ®tre d'</a>. His character helps Peter try to propose to Mary Jane. Composer <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Young" title="Christopher Young">Christopher Young</a> appears in the film as a pianist at Mary Jane's theater when she is fired, while producer <a href="/wiki/Grant_Curtis" title="Grant Curtis">Grant Curtis</a> has a cameo as the driver of an armored car that the Sandman attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-castcommentary_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-castcommentary-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"The most important thing Peter right now has to learn is that this whole concept of him as the avenger or him as the hero, he wears this red and blue outfit, with each criminal he brings to justice he's trying to pay down this debt of guilt he feels about the death of Uncle Ben. He considers himself a hero and a sinless person versus these villains that he nabs. We felt it would be a great thing for him to learn a little less black and white view of life and that he's not above these people."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">âSam Raimi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forgiveness_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-forgiveness-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>In March 2004, with <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i> being released the coming June, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> had begun developing <i>Spider-Man 3</i> for a release in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> By the release of <i>Spider-Man 2</i>, a release date for <i>Spider-Man 3</i> had been set for May 2, 2007 before production on the sequel had begun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The date was later changed to May 4, 2007. In January 2005, Sony Pictures Entertainment completed a seven-figure deal with <a href="/wiki/Screenwriter" title="Screenwriter">screenwriter</a> <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Sargent" title="Alvin Sargent">Alvin Sargent</a>, who had penned <i>Spider-Man 2</i>, to work on <i>Spider-Man 3</i> with an option to write a fourth film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Immediately after <i>Spider-Man 2'</i>s release, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Raimi" title="Ivan Raimi">Ivan Raimi</a> wrote a treatment over two months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-web-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> with Sam Raimi deciding to use the film to explore Peter learning that he is not a sinless vigilante, and that there also can be humanity in those he considers criminals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forgiveness_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-forgiveness-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">Harry Osborn</a> was brought back as Raimi wanted to conclude his storyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forgiveness_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-forgiveness-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Raimi felt that Harry would not follow his father's legacy, but be instead "somewhere between."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sandman_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Sandman (Marvel Comics)">Sandman</a> was introduced as an antagonist, as Raimi found him a visually fascinating character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forgiveness_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-forgiveness-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> While Sandman is a petty criminal in the comics, the screenwriters created a background of the character being <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Ben" title="Uncle Ben">Uncle Ben</a>'s killer to increase Peter's guilt over his death<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arad_IGN_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-arad_IGN-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and challenge his simplistic perception of the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forgiveness_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-forgiveness-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall, Raimi described the film as being about Peter, Mary Jane, Harry, and the Sandman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beef_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-beef-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> with Peter's journey being one of <a href="/wiki/Forgiveness" title="Forgiveness">forgiveness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-closeup_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-closeup-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Raimi wanted another villain, and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a> was involved in negotiations to play the <a href="/wiki/Vulture_(comics)" title="Vulture (comics)">Vulture</a> before the character was cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-web-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a> convinced Raimi to include Venom, a character whose perceived "lack of humanity" had initially been criticized by Sam Raimi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-igncon_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-igncon-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Venom's alter-ego, Eddie Brock, already had a minor role in the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grantfour_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-grantfour-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Arad told the director that Venom had a strong <a href="/wiki/Fan_(person)" title="Fan (person)">fan base</a>, so Raimi included the character to please them,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beef_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-beef-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and even began to appreciate the character himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-igncon_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-igncon-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's version of the character is an <a href="/wiki/Amalgamation_(fiction)" title="Amalgamation (fiction)">amalgamation</a> of Venom stories. Eddie Brock, Jr., the human part of Venom, serves as a mirror to Peter Parker, with both characters having similar jobs and romantic interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-igncon_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-igncon-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Brock's actions as a journalist in <i>Spider-Man 3</i> also represent contemporary themes of <a href="/wiki/Paparazzi" title="Paparazzi">paparazzi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_journalism" title="Tabloid journalism">tabloid journalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inner_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-inner-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The producers also suggested adding rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Love_interest" title="Love interest">love interest</a> <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stacy" title="Gwen Stacy">Gwen Stacy</a>, filling in an "other girl" type that Raimi already created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beef_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-beef-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> With so many additions, Sargent soon found his script so complex that he considered splitting it into two films, but abandoned the idea when he could not create a successful intermediate climax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-web-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Camera crews spent ten days from November 5, 2005 to November 18, 2005, to film sequences that would involve intense <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual effects</a> so <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Imageworks" title="Sony Pictures Imageworks">Sony Pictures Imageworks</a> could begin work on the shots early in the project. The same steps had been taken for <i>Spider-Man 2</i> to begin producing visual effects early for sequences involving the villain <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Octopus" title="Doctor Octopus">Doctor Octopus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photo_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-photo-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> for <i>Spider-Man 3</i> began on January 16, 2006 and wrapped in July 2006 after over a hundred days of filming. The team filmed in Los Angeles until May 19, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photo_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-photo-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In spring 2006, film <a href="/wiki/Location_manager" title="Location manager">location manager</a> Peter Martorano brought camera crews to <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> due to the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cleveland_Film_Commission" title="Greater Cleveland Film Commission">Greater Cleveland Film Commission</a> offering production space at the city's <a href="/wiki/Convention_center" title="Convention center">convention center</a> at no cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In Cleveland, they shot the battle between Spider-Man and Sandman in the armored car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-web-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Afterwards, the team moved to Manhattan, where filming took place at various locations, including <a href="/wiki/One_Chase_Manhattan_Plaza" title="One Chase Manhattan Plaza">One Chase Manhattan Plaza</a>, from May 26, 2006 until July 1, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photo_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-photo-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Shooting placed a strain on Raimi, who often had to move between several units to complete the picture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-web-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Shooting was also difficult for cinematographer Bill Pope, as the symbiote Spider-Man, Venom, and the New Goblin were costumed in black during <a href="/wiki/Stage_combat" title="Stage combat">fight scenes</a> taking place at night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After August, <a href="/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking)" title="Pick-up (filmmaking)">pick-ups</a> were conducted as Raimi sought to film more action scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The film then wrapped in October, although in the following month, additional <a href="/wiki/Special_effect" title="Special effect">special effects</a> shots were taken to finalize the production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dunst_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-dunst-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> At the start of 2007, there were further <a href="/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking)" title="Pick-up (filmmaking)">pick-up shots</a> regarding the resolution of Sandman's story, amounting to four different versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sense_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-sense-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S3_sandman_punch.jpg"><img alt="Spider-Man punches Sandman, and his fist is seen on the other side of his chest, with sand blowing through the hole" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="182" data-file-width="270" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/30/S3_sandman_punch.jpg/220px-S3_sandman_punch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/30/S3_sandman_punch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/30/S3_sandman_punch.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S3_sandman_punch.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Amputee boxer <a href="/wiki/Baxter_Humby" title="Baxter Humby">Baxter Humby</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Spider-Man</a>, throws a computer-generated punch through the chest of <a href="/wiki/Sandman_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Sandman (Marvel Comics)">Sandman</a>, portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Haden_Church" title="Thomas Haden Church">Thomas Haden Church</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Dykstra" title="John Dykstra">John Dykstra</a>, who won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Visual Effects">Academy Award for Visual Effects</a> for his work on <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i>, declined to work on the third film as visual effects supervisor. Dykstra's colleague, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Stokdyk" title="Scott Stokdyk">Scott Stokdyk</a>, took his place as supervisor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> leading two hundred programmers at Sony Pictures Imageworks. This group designed specific <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">computer programs</a> that did not exist when <i>Spider-Man 3</i> began production, creating nine hundred visual effects shots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sand_star_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-sand_star-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venom_concept_art.jpg"><img alt="Concept art for Venom's costume, which is a black-white version of Spider-Man's suit, but more muscular and with an open mouth with sharp teeth" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="200" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3c/Venom_concept_art.jpg/120px-Venom_concept_art.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3c/Venom_concept_art.jpg/180px-Venom_concept_art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/3c/Venom_concept_art.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venom_concept_art.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Concept art of the <a href="/wiki/Venom_(comics)" title="Venom (comics)">Venom</a> suit, which possesses a webbing motif, unlike the comics, in order to show the symbiote's control and represent the character as a twisted <a href="/wiki/Foil_(literature)" title="Foil (literature)">foil</a> to Spider-Man.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the innovative visual effects for the film, Stokdyk created a miniature of a skyscraper section at 1:16 scale with <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> Studios' <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hunter_(visual_effects_supervisor)" title="Ian Hunter (visual effects supervisor)">Ian Hunter</a> and David Sanger. Stokdyk chose to design the miniature instead of using <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> so damage done to the building could be portrayed realistically and timely without guesswork involving <a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">computer models</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-answered_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-answered-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, to Sony Imageworks, <a href="/wiki/Cafe_FX" title="Cafe FX">Cafe FX</a> provided visual effects for the crane disaster scene when Spider-Man rescues Gwen Stacy, as well as shots in the climactic battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> To understand the effects of sand for the Sandman, experiments were done with twelve types of sand, such as splashing, launching it at stuntmen, and pouring it over ledges. The results were mimicked on the computer to create the visual effects for Sandman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sand_star_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-sand_star-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> For scenes involving visual effects, Thomas Haden Church was super-imposed onto the screen, where computer-generated imagery was then applied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enter_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-enter-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> With sand as a possible hazard in scenes that buried actors, ground-up corncobs were used as a substitute instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premiere_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of its resemblance to the substance, sand from <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> was used as the model for the CG sand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sand_star_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-sand_star-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> In a fight where Spider-Man punches through Sandman's chest, <a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">amputee</a> martial arts expert <a href="/wiki/Baxter_Humby" title="Baxter Humby">Baxter Humby</a> took Tobey Maguire's place in filming the scene. Humby, whose right hand was amputated at birth, helped deliver the intended effect of punching through Sandman's chest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Whereas the symbiote suit worn in the comics by Spider-Man was a plain black affair with a large white spider on the front and back, the design was changed for the film to become a black version of Spider-Man's traditional costume, complete with webbing <a href="/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)" title="Motif (visual arts)">motif</a>. As a consequence of this, the suit <a href="/wiki/Topher_Grace" title="Topher Grace">Topher Grace</a> wore as Venom also bore the webbing motif; as producer <a href="/wiki/Grant_Curtis" title="Grant Curtis">Grant Curtis</a> noted, "itâs the Spider-Man suit, but twisted and mangled in its own right."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the motif gave a sense of life to the symbiote, giving it the appearance of gripping onto the character's body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> When animating the symbiote, Raimi did not want it to resemble a spider or an octopus, and to give it a sense of character. The CG model is made of many separate strands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> When animating Venom himself, animators observed footage of <a href="/wiki/Big_cat" title="Big cat">big cats</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">cheetahs</a> for the character's agile movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Originally, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Elfman" title="Danny Elfman">Danny Elfman</a>, the composer for the previous installments, did not plan to return for the third installment of <i>Spider-Man</i> because of difficulties with director Sam Raimi. Elfman said that he had a "miserable experience" working with Raimi on <i>Spider-Man 2</i> and could not comfortably adapt his music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Young" title="Christopher Young">Christopher Young</a> was then announced to score <i>Spider-Man 3</i> in Elfman's absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2006, however, producer Grant Curtis announced that Elfman had begun collaborating with Christopher Young on the music for <i>Spider-Man 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sandman's theme uses "two <a href="/wiki/Contrabass_saxophone" title="Contrabass saxophone">contrabass</a> <a href="/wiki/Saxophone" title="Saxophone">saxophones</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Contrabass_clarinet" title="Contrabass clarinet">contrabass</a> <a href="/wiki/Clarinet" title="Clarinet">clarinets</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Contrabassoon" title="Contrabassoon">contrabass bassoons</a> and eight very low <a href="/wiki/French_horn" title="French horn">French horns</a>" to sound "low, aggressive and heavy". Young described Venom's theme as "Vicious, my instructions on that one were that heâs the devil personified. His theme is much more demonic sounding."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scorekeeper_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-scorekeeper-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Venom's theme uses eight French horns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swingmusic_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-swingmusic-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Raimi approved the new themes during their first performance, but rejected the initial music to the birth of Sandman, finding it too monstrous and not tragic enough. Young had to recompose much of his score at a later stage, as the producers felt there were not enough themes from the previous films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scorekeeper_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-scorekeeper-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Ultimately, new themes for the love story, Aunt May, and Mary Jane were dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swingmusic_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-swingmusic-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="Tobey Maguire, in a suit, greets fans behind a security barrier. Most of the attendants hold cameras." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/200px-Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/300px-Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/400px-Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tobey_Maguire_greets_fans_at_Spiderman_3_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a> greets fans at the premiere in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queens,_New_York" title="Queens, New York">Queens, New York</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Spider-Man 3</i> had its world premiere at Toho Cinemas Roppongi Hills in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> on April 16, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tokyo_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The film held its UK premiere on April 23, 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Leicester_Square" title="Odeon Leicester Square">Odeon Leicester Square</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and the U.S. premiere took place at the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> on April 30, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Spider-Man 3</i> was commercially released in sixteen territories on May 1, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snares_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-snares-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was released in Japan on May 1, 2007, three days prior to the American commercial release, to coincide with Japan's <a href="/wiki/Golden_Week_(Japan)" title="Golden Week (Japan)">Golden Week</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tokyo_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Spider-Man 3</i> was also released in China on May 3, 2007 to circumvent market growth of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement_of_audio-visual_works" title="Copyright infringement of audio-visual works">pirated copies</a> of the film. The studio's release of a film in China before its domestic release was a first for Sony Pictures Releasing International.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> By May 6, 2007, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> opened in 107 countries around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snares_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-snares-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film was commercially released in the United States on May 4, 2007 in a North American record total of 4,253 theaters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-records-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> including fifty-three <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The record number of theaters was later beaten by <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i>, which was released in 4,362 theaters in the United Statesâ109 more than <i>Spider-Man 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Tracking data a month before the U.S. release reflected over 90% awareness and over 20% first choice among moviegoers, statistics that estimated an opening weekend of over $100 million for <i>Spider-Man 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Online tickets for <i>Spider-Man 3</i> were reported on April 23, 2007 to have been purchased at a faster rateâthree times at Movietickets.com and four times at <a href="/wiki/Fandango_(ticket_service)" title="Fandango (ticket service)">Fandango</a>âthan online ticket sales for <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 2, 2007, Fandango reported the sales rate as six times greater than the rate for <i>Spider-Man 2</i>. The strong ticket sales caused theaters to add 3:00 AM showings following the May 4, 2007 midnight showing to accommodate the demand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/FX_(TV_channel)" title="FX (TV channel)">FX</a> channel signed a five-year deal for the television rights to <i>Spider-Man 3</i>, which they began airing in 2009. The price was based on the film's box office performance, with an option for three opportunities for Sony to sell the rights to one or more other broadcast networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3_(video_game)" title="Spider-Man 3 (video game)">Spider-Man 3 (video game)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3_(soundtrack)" title="Spider-Man 3 (soundtrack)">Spider-Man 3 (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, the hometown of Spider-Man's <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe" title="Fictional universe">fictional universe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">tourist attractions</a> arranged events and exhibits on April 30, 2007 to lead up to the release of <i>Spider-Man 3</i>. The unique campaign include a spider exhibit at the <a href="/wiki/American_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="American Museum of Natural History">American Museum of Natural History</a>, workshops on baby spider plants at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Botanical_Garden" title="New York Botanical Garden">New York Botanical Garden</a>, Green Goblin mask-making workshop at the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Manhattan" title="Children's Museum of Manhattan">Children's Museum of Manhattan</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Scavenger_hunt" title="Scavenger hunt">scavenger hunt</a> and a bug show at <a href="/wiki/Central_Park_Zoo" title="Central Park Zoo">Central Park Zoo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, which holds the license for Marvel characters, released several toys to <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie-in</a> with the film. They include a deluxe spinning web blaster, along with several lines of <a href="/wiki/Action_figure" title="Action figure">action figures</a> aimed at both children and collectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Toys of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">Green Goblin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Octopus" title="Doctor Octopus">Doctor Octopus</a> from the first two films have been re-released to match the smaller scale of the new figures, as have been toys of the <a href="/wiki/Lizard_(comics)" title="Lizard (comics)">Lizard</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mac_Gargan" title="Mac Gargan">Scorpion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kraven_the_Hunter" title="Kraven the Hunter">Kraven the Hunter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rhino_(comics)" title="Rhino (comics)">Rhino</a> in a style reminiscent of the films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Techno_Source" title="Techno Source">Techno Source</a> created interactive toys, including a "hand-held Battle Tronics device that straps to the inside of a player's wrist and mimics Spidey's web-slinging motions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Japanese Medicom Toy Corporation produced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectible" title="Collectible">collectibles</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Sideshow_Collectibles" title="Sideshow Collectibles">Sideshow Collectibles</a> distributed in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film received mixed to positive reception from critics, in contrast to the previous two films' highly positive reviews. On the <a href="/wiki/Film_criticism" title="Film criticism">movie review</a> aggregator site <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> has a 63% approval rating based on 244 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> has received a score of 59/100 based on 40 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Movies" title="Yahoo! Movies">Yahoo! Movies</a>, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> is graded a B- among 14 film critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Manohla_Dargis" title="Manohla Dargis">Manohla Dargis</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> deplored the film's pacing as "mostly just plods" and a lack of humor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> gave the film only 2 out of 4 stars, feeling, "for every slam-bang action sequence, there are far too many sluggish scenes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Edelstein" title="David Edelstein">David Edelstein</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine misses the "centrifugal threat" of <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Molina" title="Alfred Molina">Alfred Molina's</a> character, adding that "the three villains here donât add up to one <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Octopus" title="Doctor Octopus">Doc Ock</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> (referring to <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Molina" title="Alfred Molina">Alfred Molina</a>'s portrayal of the character in <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i>). <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a> felt director Sam Raimi "overreached his grasp" by allowing so many villains, specifically saying, "Venom is one bad guy too many."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> gave the film 2 out of four stars and thought Church never expressed how Sandman felt about his new powers, something Molina, as Doc Ock in <i>Spider-Man 2</i>, did "with a vengeance"; he said the film was "a mess," with too many villains, subplots, romantic misunderstandings, conversations and "street crowds looking high into the air and shouting 'oooh!' this way, then swiveling and shouting 'aaah!' that way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a>'s</i> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Lane" title="Anthony Lane">Anthony Lane</a> gave the film a mildly positive review, summarizing it as "shambles" which "makes the rules up as it goes along."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, Roger Friedman of <a href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News</a> called the film a "4 star opera", noting that while long, there was plenty of humor and action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Andy Khouri of <a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Resources" title="Comic Book Resources">Comic Book Resources</a> praised the film as "easily the most complex and deftly orchestrated superhero epic ever filmed [...] despite the enormous amount of characters, action and <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">sci-fi</a> superhero plot going on in this film, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> never feels weighted down, tedious or boring."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Ross" title="Jonathan Ross">Jonathan Ross</a>, a big fan of the comic books, felt the film was the best of the trilogy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> commended the filmmakers for their ability to "dramatize feelings of angst and personal betrayal worthy of an <a href="/wiki/Ingmar_Bergman" title="Ingmar Bergman">Ingmar Bergman</a> film, and then to dress them up in gaudy comic-book colors".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Morris" title="Wesley Morris">Wesley Morris</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i>, who gave the film 4 out of 5 stars, wrote that it was a well-made, fresh film, but would leave the viewer "overfulfilled".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Jonathan Dean of <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Film" title="Total Film">Total Film</a></i> felt the film's complex plot helped the film's pacing, in that, "it rarely feels disjointed or loose [...] Spider-Man cements its shelf-life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> named the Sandman as the eighth best computer-generated film character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>John Hartl of <i><a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a></i> gave <i>Spider-Man 3</i> a positive review, but stated that it has some flaws such as having "too many storylines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> His opinion is echoed by <i><a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">Houston Chronicle's</a></i> Amy Biancolli who complained that "the script is busy with so many supporting characters and plot detours that the series' charming idiosyncrasy is sometimes lost in the noise."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Jack Matthews of <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i> thought the film was too devoted to the "quiet conversations" of Peter and Mary Jane, but that fans would not be disappointed by the action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, Sean Burns of <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Weekly" title="Philadelphia Weekly">Philadelphia Weekly</a></i> felt that the director "substituted scope and scale for the warmth and wit that made those two previous pictures so memorable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Both the <a href="/wiki/35th_Annie_Awards" title="35th Annie Awards">35th Annie Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/61st_British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="61st British Academy Film Awards">61st British Academy Film Awards</a> gave this movie one nomination, the former for Best Animated Effects and the latter for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Visual Effects</a>. <i>Spider-Man 3</i> did not win any of the four Visual Effects Society Awards nominations it received. Dunst's and Maguire's performances earned them each one nomination from the National Movie Awards. She also received another nomination for Favorite Movie Actress from the <a href="/wiki/2008_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2008 Kids' Choice Awards">2008 Kids' Choice Awards</a> ceremony. The movie fared better at the <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a>, amounting a total of seven nominations, varying from Choice Movie: Villain (for Grace) to Choice Movie: Dance (for Maguire) and Choice Movie: Liplock (shared between Dunst and Maguire).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Spider-Man 3</i> earned $336,530,303 in North America and $554,341,323 in other countries for a worldwide total of $890,871,626.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Worldwide, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">32nd highest-grossing film</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2007_in_film" title="2007 in film">third highest-grossing 2007 film</a>, the highest-grossing film of <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film#Raimi_Trilogy" title="Spider-Man in film">Sam Raimi's <i>Spider-Man</i> trilogy</a> and was the highest-grossing film distributed by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Sony/Columbia</a> until 2012's <i><a href="/wiki/Skyfall" title="Skyfall">Skyfall</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The film set a worldwide single-day record ($104 million) on its first Friday and broke its own record again on Saturday ($117.6 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_breaking_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Record_breaking-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> It also set a worldwide opening-weekend record, with $381.7 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_breaking_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Record_breaking-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> which now ranks as the fifth largest (first surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's IMAX screenings reached $20 million in 30 days, faster than any other 2D film remastered in the format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In North America, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Not_adjusted_for_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">twenty-ninth highest grossing film</a>, the third highest-grossing film of the <i>Spider-Man</i> series, the third highest-grossing film distributed by Sony/Columbia and the highest-grossing 2007 film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> It was released in 4,252 theaters (about 10,300 screens) on Friday, May 4, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> It set an opening- and single-day record with $59,841,919<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> (both were first surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>). This included $10 million from midnight showings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Spider-Man 3</i> then set an opening-weekend record with $151,116,516 (first surpassed by <i>The Dark Knight</i>), a record for the weekend per-theater average with $35,540 per theater (first surpassed by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hannah_Montana_%26_Miley_Cyrus:_Best_of_Both_Worlds_Concert" title="Hannah Montana &amp; Miley Cyrus: Best of Both Worlds Concert">Hannah Montana &amp; Miley Cyrus: Best of Both Worlds Concert</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> and an IMAX opening-weekend record with $4.8 million (first surpassed by <i>The Dark Knight</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The film set record Friday<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> and Sunday grosses<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> and achieved the largest cumulative gross through its second, third and fourth day of release (all were first surpassed by <i>The Dark Knight</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> It also set a record Saturday gross (surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Marvel's The Avengers</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Outside North America, it is the twenty-third highest-grossing film, the highest-grossing film of Sam Raimi's <i>Spider-Man</i> trilogy and the third highest-grossing film distributed by Sony/Columbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> On its opening day (Tuesday, May 1, 2007), <i>Spider-Man 3</i> grossed $29.2 million from 16 territories, an 86% increase from the intake of <i>Spider-Man 2</i> on its first day of release. In 10 of the 16 territories, <i>Spider-Man 3</i> set new opening-day records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snares_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-snares-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> These territories are Japan, South Korea, Hong Kong, Thailand, Malaysia, Singapore, Taiwan, the Philippines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-records-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> France<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA-GER_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FRA-GER-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> and Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> In Germany, the film surpassed the opening day gross of <i>Spider-Man 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA-GER_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA-GER-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> During its six-day opening weekend (through its first Sunday), the film earned $230.5 million from 107 markets, finishing #1 in all of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_breaking_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-Record_breaking-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Spider-Man 3</i> set opening-weekend records in 29 markets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_breaking_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-Record_breaking-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> including Italy, China, South Korea (the latter was first surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> India, Singapore, Philippines, Hong Kong, Thailand, Malaysia, Taiwan, Indonesia, Mexico, Brazil, Argentina, Colombia, Peru. However, many of these records were achieved thanks to its six-day opening, while previous record-holders in some countries opened over the traditional three-day weekend (traditional two-day, four-day or five-day weekend in other countries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Spider-Man 3</i> was in first place at the box office outside North America for three consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_video">Home video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Home video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Spider-Man 3</i> was released on <a href="/wiki/DVD_region_code#.5B.5BRegion_4.5D.5D" title="DVD region code">Region 4 DVD</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anamorphic_widescreen" title="Anamorphic widescreen">anamorphic widescreen</a>) in Australia on September 18, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/DVD_region_code#.5B.5BRegion_2.5D.5D" title="DVD region code">Region 2</a> in the United Kingdom, the film was released on October 15, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Spider-Man 3</i> was released on DVD in <a href="/wiki/DVD_region_code#.5B.5BRegion_1.5D.5D" title="DVD region code">Region 1</a> territories on October 30, 2007. The film is available in one-disc and two-disc editions, on both standard and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> formats, as well as packages with the previous films and a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PSP</a> release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Dunst" title="Kirsten Dunst">Kirsten Dunst</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Haden_Church" title="Thomas Haden Church">Thomas Haden Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Topher_Grace" title="Topher Grace">Topher Grace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryce_Dallas_Howard" title="Bryce Dallas Howard">Bryce Dallas Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Ziskin" title="Laura Ziskin">Laura Ziskin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grant_Curtis" title="Grant Curtis">Grant Curtis</a> are among those who contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Audio_commentary" title="Audio commentary">audio commentaries</a>.</p>
<p>Sony announced plans to create "one of the largest" marketing campaigns in Hollywood for the October 30, 2007 release of the DVD. Beginning with a partnership with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papa_Johns" title="Papa Johns">Papa Johns</a>, Sony printed close to 8.5 billion impressions for pizza boxes, television, radio, and online ads. Sony also worked with <a href="/wiki/Pringles" title="Pringles">Pringles</a> Potato Crisp, <a href="/wiki/Blu-Tack" title="Blu-Tack">Blu-Tack</a>, Jolly Time Pop Corn, and <a href="/wiki/Nutella" title="Nutella">Nutella</a>. Sony's Vice President of marketing, Jennifer Anderson, stated the studio spend approximately 15% to 25% of its marketing budget on digital ad campaigns; from this, Papa Johns sent text messages to mobile phones with ads. Anderson stated that there would be three sweepstakes held for consumers, where they would be able to win prizes from Sony and its promotional partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, the film grossed more than $124 million on DVD sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> It also grossed more than $43.76 million on DVD/Home Video Rentals in 11 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the DVD sales results of this film did not meet industry expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)</a></div>
<p>In 2007, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spider-Man_4" title="Spider-Man 4">Spider-Man 4</a></i> entered development, with Raimi attached to direct and Maguire, Dunst and other cast members set to reprise their roles. Both a fourth and a fifth film were planned and at one time the idea of shooting the two sequels concurrently was under consideration. However, Raimi stated in March 2009 that only the fourth film was in development at that time and that if there were fifth and sixth films, those two films would actually be a continuation of each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Vanderbilt" title="James Vanderbilt">James Vanderbilt</a> was hired in October 2007 to pen the screenplay after initial reports in early 2007 that Sony Pictures was in contact with <a href="/wiki/David_Koepp" title="David Koepp">David Koepp</a>, who wrote the first <i>Spider-Man</i> film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-script-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The script was subsequently rewritten by <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer</a>-winning playwright <a href="/wiki/David_Lindsay-Abaire" title="David Lindsay-Abaire">David Lindsay-Abaire</a> and rewritten again by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Ross" title="Gary Ross">Gary Ross</a> in October 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Sony also engaged Vanderbilt to write scripts for <i>Spider-Man 5</i> and <i>Spider-Man 6</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-script-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Raimi expressed interest in portraying the transformation of Dr. Curt Connors into his villainous alter-ego, the <a href="/wiki/Lizard_(comics)" title="Lizard (comics)">Lizard</a>; the character's actor <a href="/wiki/Dylan_Baker" title="Dylan Baker">Dylan Baker</a> and producer Grant Curtis were also enthusiastic about the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raimivillains_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-raimivillains-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> It was reported in December 2009 that <a href="/wiki/John_Malkovich" title="John Malkovich">John Malkovich</a> was in negotiations to play <a href="/wiki/Vulture_(comics)" title="Vulture (comics)">Vulture</a> and that <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> would play <a href="/wiki/Black_Cat_(comics)" title="Black Cat (comics)">Felicia Hardy</a>, though she would not have transformed into the Black Cat as in the comics. Instead, Raimi's Felicia was expected to become a brand-new superpowered figure called the Vulturess. However, several years later Raimi stated that Anne Hathaway was going to be Black Cat if <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spider-Man_4" title="Spider-Man 4">Spider-Man 4</a></i> had been made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sony Pictures announced in January 2010 that plans for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spider-Man_4" title="Spider-Man 4">Spider-Man 4</a></i> had been cancelled due to Raimi's withdrawal from the project. Raimi reportedly ended his participation due to his doubt that he could meet the planned May 6, 2011 release date while at the same time upholding the film creatively. Raimi purportedly went through four iterations of the script with different screenwriters and still "hated it".</p>
<p>The next film in the franchise, a reboot of the series, called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">The Amazing Spider-Man</a></i> was released on July 3, 2012, with <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Garfield" title="Andrew Garfield">Andrew Garfield</a> as Peter Parker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reboot_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-reboot-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2015, Sony Pictures and Marvel Studios announced that Spider-Man will appear in the Marvel Cinematic Universe (MCU), with the character appearing in an MCU film and Sony releasing a <i>Spider-Man</i> film produced by Feige and Pascal on July 28, 2017. Sony will continue to finance, distribute, own and have final creative control of the <i>Spider-Man</i> films. Marvel Studios will also explore opportunities to integrate other characters of the Marvel Cinematic Universe into future <i>Spider-Man</i> films. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported that the new incarnation of the character would appear in 2016's <i>Captain America: Civil War</i>. In February 2015, it was later announced that Logan Lerman and Dylan O'Brien are both being eyed for the role of Spider-Man.</p>
